Round 7 Feature Match - Josh Utter-Leyton vs. Ben Rasmussen
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*

Josh Utter-Leyton has been having a great couple years and has really made a name for himself. Recently, he finished second at Pro Tour Philadelphia, Top 8 at Grand Prix Dallas and Nashville, and, don't forget, he was the US National Champion of 2010. Yeah, he's made quite a name indeed. He's looking quite suave in his snazzy ChannelFireball&gt; sweatshirt.


Ben Rasmussen, Madison, Wisconsin staple, and Grand Prix Indianapolis Top 8er, who lines his playmate with endless PTQ Top 8 pins, has a decidedly less formal approach. Though he's no longer wearing his trademark Metallica hat (I think it simply imploded due to use), he's donning a shirt that reads, "Science flies you to the moon; Religion flies you into buildings." I ask him about the hat and he said it's alive and as well as can be expected, but it's taking a bit of a breather.


**Game 1** 


[Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul) and [Walking Corpse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Walking+Corpse) started the game for Rasmussen. Utter-Leyton had a [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), [Deranged Assistant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deranged+Assistant) and a [Selhoff Occultist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selhoff+Occultist). The 2/3 proved just good enough to dissuade Rasmussen's 2-powered friends from attacking. Utter-Leyton pressed the issue with a turn-four [Pitchburn Devils](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pitchburn+Devils). The Assistant was really doing his job to power up the curve.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Ben%20Rasmussen.JPG)
*Ben Rasmussen* 

Rasmussen dropped land four, now showing two [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp)s an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) and a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) against similar colors from Utter-Leyton. The Devils crashed in and traded with a [Typhoid Rats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Typhoid+Rats), dragging the Corpse back to the grave with him.


[Makeshift Mauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Makeshift+Mauler) was Utter-Leyton's follow-up. Rasmussen was down to one creature against Utter-Leyton's four, and his hand was mostly land. He used the non-land portion to [Sever the Bloodline](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sever+the+Bloodline) of the new 4/5 zombie. And just when Rasmussen seemed all right, the Delver finally flipped into an [Insectile Aberration](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Insectile+Aberration). Utter-Leyton sunk Rassy-ras to 14 and cast a [Skirsdag High Priest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skirsdag+High+Priest).


Even with the Wisconsinite's [Village Cannibals](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Village+Cannibals), Utter-Leyton was still ahead on the board, and his hand had a [Desperate Ravings](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ravings), [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) and an [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) in it. Rasmussen's had two land. The totals went to 11-18.


Rasmussen flashed back his [Sever the Bloodline](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sever+the+Bloodline) on the High Priest, allowing Utter-Leyton to respond by triggering his High Priest's morbid with a [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) on the Cannibals. Next turn, the new 5/5 Demon, the 3/2 flyer, and the 2/3 miller made the scores 3-18. Rasmussen's [Think Twice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Think+Twice) netted a second [Think Twice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Think+Twice) (a little ironic), but that was it. Those spells wouldn't stop the steamroll coming at him the next turn. Though it might make me think of a certain 90s Alanis Morissette song.


Josh Utter-Leyton 1 – 0 Ben Rasmussen


**Game 2** 


Rasmussen led this game with a [Typhoid Rats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Typhoid+Rats), [Selhoff Occultist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selhoff+Occultist), and all three [Grixis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grixis)-aligned lands. Utter-Leyton simply cast a turn-four [Moon Heron](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moon+Heron). He was down to 15 before attacking with the Heron. The 2-for-1 [Hill Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hill+Giant), [Pitchburn Devils](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pitchburn+Devils) followed closely behind the attack, and now Rasmussen, still stuck on three land, was in danger of falling behind. He used a Devil's Play to take out the flyer which blunted Utter-Leyton's offense, but the former Nation Champ had more than enough defense in his hand to make up for it. A [Sever the Bloodline](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sever+the+Bloodline), an [Armored Skaab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armored+Skaab) and a [Selhoff Occultist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selhoff+Occultist) all waited in between his fingers. The Occultist came down before the Devil attack, then Utter-Leyton dropped a land and cast his Skaab.


Rasmussen's hand was filled with goodies. A [Sever the Bloodline](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sever+the+Bloodline) of his own, a [Garruk Relentless](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk+Relentless) and a bevy of creatures, but the land to cast any of them were scarce. He used [Silent Departure](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silent+Departure) to delay the Devils, then, drawing a land on his next turn, Severed the Devils' Bloodline. If the Devils had a fee tail on any of their property, it would pass to the next future-interest holder – if you know what I mean.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Josh%20Utter%20Leyton.JPG)
*Josh Utter Leyton* 

Utter-Leyton didn't even blink. Not at my obscure property law reference, nor the actual Severing of his Devils' Bloodline. He drew, dropped a [Deranged Assistant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deranged+Assistant) and a [Makeshift Mauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Makeshift+Mauler). A veritable wall of blue creatures now stood in front of him. (Important to note, however, this wall does not fly. So the new [Moon Heron](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moon+Heron) from Rasmussen would get through unimpeded.) Rasmussen's two [Typhoid Rats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Typhoid+Rats) proved too juicy of a target for Utter-Leyton to avoid, and used his [Sever the Bloodline](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sever+the+Bloodline) to eradicate their fee tails as well (and their rat tails).


After a bounce, Utter-Leyton's last two cards in-hand were [Fortress Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fortress+Crab) and [Makeshift Mauler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Makeshift+Mauler). They both came down to remake a bigger and better wall of blue. Rasmussen meek-looking [Walking Corpse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Walking+Corpse) and Occultist were all that remained after a [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) took out his spectral bird.


An uncastable [Morkrut Banshee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Morkrut+Banshee) and [Moan of the Unhallowed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moan+of+the+Unhallowed) were stranded in Rasmussen's hand. And if he didn't do something soon, the bevy of big blue butts make the totals more lopsided than they already were at 13-10 for Utter-Leyton. The next attack sunk Rasmussen to 6 and lost his Corpse in the process. The second swamp was finally found after some Selhoff triggers and the two 2/2 zombies came down after a distinct Moaning sound.


But hey, remember those [Sever the Bloodline](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sever+the+Bloodline)s sitting in each players' graveyards? I don't think Rasmussen did. Utter-Leyton simply dropped a land and pointed the black card at both of the Zombie tokens and Rasmussen had to scoop them up.


Josh Utter-Leyton 2 – 0 Ben Rasmussen




Saturday, 7:05 p.m. - Jeff Zandi and the Texas Guildmages: Clear Eyes, Full Hearts, Can’t Lose!
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Michael%20Friedman.jpg)
*Michael Friedman* 

Origins Game Fair, Fort [Wort, Boggart Auntie](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Wort%252C%2BBoggart%2BAuntie)h, Texas, 1993. That's where Jeff Zandi first encountered **Magic**. "I'm pretty sure that was one of the first places you could encounter it. They didn't actually have any cards, but there was a brochure." I sat with him between rounds, watching him reshuffle his sideboard out of his deck. He had just won a long round, and was as happy as ever. In fact, he was so happy, he started talking to me and introduced himself before I had a chance to do the same myself and ask if I could interview him.


His love affair with the game started a little while after that first encounter back at Origins. It began with a Unlimited Starter deck and a cutout panel in a rulebook – allowing to send away and become a member of the DCI equivalent of the day. "I received a hand-laminated, hand-written card with my four-digit DCI number." Fast-forward fourteen years, and his playgroup and team, the Texas Guildmages, have just held their 736th weekly meeting. Skipping weeks only for holidays, the team has been meeting for the better part of 15 years. **Magic** in the Dallas region runs deep and true.


With currently 35 lifetime members, though rarely going over an active member number of 8, the goal of the Texas Guildmages was modest: to always have eight people consistently excited about playing **Magic** and striving to improve. The most illustrious alumni of the crew are probably Neil Reeves and superstar Dave Williams, but the Guildmage history goes further than that. "When we first formed, Dave was fourteen. There was time when we had seven and just needed an eighth and so Dave became that eighth."


The small size invariably leads to some elitism. "Some people call us clique-y, but there's a surefire way to become a Guildmage: Just keep contributing and just keep coming." Zandi said it's pretty funny because since the Guildmages have bit of a reputation at this point, when people come over to play for the first time, they are always excited, but then a little bit disappointed at the realization that it's just dudes playing **Magic**. But kids, that's what it's all about: Dudes playing **Magic** (non-gender specific use of "dude", of course). And with the consistency of membership activity that the Guildmages present it'd be hard to deny their significant influence on the community and an aspect of **Magic** sociability that every community should have.


As I talked to Zandi about his involvement in the Texas **Magic** community, younger players, some whom I recognized, some I did not, came up giving Zandi updates on their performance. Sometimes he'd be hit on the shoulder and hear "2-0!" shouted in passing, other times he'd be regaled by a sweet-beat story. As we talked, Texas **Magic**ian and writer extraordinaire Kyle Sanchez sat down an contributed to the story telling. Zandi sure is a part of something good.


He's not without a twinge of sadness about the team though. He said that the team's been very good, fantastic even, at getting people onto the Pro Tour, but then they get involved in larger communities than the small northern Texas team. However, it's exactly things like achievement and change that a) bring more interest and intrigue to the team, and b) allow younger players to become of a part of the community and get more involved. If the same original eight team members of Texas Guildmage were still the only eight, well, who knows where Dave Williams would be?


Zandi often mentions players and friends, saying that even though they aren't members of the team, there are frequent and numerous guests who take part in the Guildmages' meetings and happenings. And he'd know exactly who's attended over the years. Because, in addition to the group's stellar track record for meetings, Zandi has a stellar track record for note-taking. He's written down every single match of **Magic** he's played. Period. This tactic started on pencil and paper, eventually moved to a Palm pilot (on which he created an app to allow him to download the content to a spreadsheet) and now on that whole mobile device thing or whatever kids are using nowadays. He's also taken meticulous detailed notes about meetings. A quick look at his notes from the 736th Guildmage meeting showed stats of all the attendees. Their lifetime number of attendances, matches played, and tons of more info therein. What does he use said information for, you ask? Well a) good question. And b) data. It's no secret Zandi loves data. And I can imagine the ultimate spreadsheet of his entire **Magic** career adorning a wall one day.


However, there's also a very real practical application: Anniversaries. "Not too long ago a team member had his 100th team meeting, so we made him a cake." It's little tidbits like these that really build that tight-knit sense of community **Magic** thrives on. And he's not just community-minded when it comes to his playgroup, he's also a level two judge, and he's written several articles about the importance of playgroups and the social mentality.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Jeff%20Zandi.jpg)
*Jeff Zandi* 

Jeff Zandi has been a mainstay in the strong world of Texas **Magic** which says a lot – Texas is big, and it's idiosyncratic. The players here have their own sense of the world, just like Texas proper. As Sanchez extolled, they're known for building their own decks, loving Rock decks, and staying the hell away from combo. "It doesn't matter how good the deck is, if it's combo, they're probably not going to play it," Zandi added. And just looking around the room at the myriad Texas shirts and apparel, whether they be school-affiliated, sports-affiliated or just state-affiliated, it's safe to say Texans are proud, strong, and just pretty awesome. I think all those words describe Jeff Zandi pretty well. He's proud, strong, and pretty awesome. And a great bastion for Texas **Magic** to the world.




Round 8 Feature Match - Paul Rietzl vs. Brian Kibler
----------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

Brian Kibler is returning to the scene of the crime, so to speak, as he revisits Austin for the first time since winning Pro Tour Austin IN DATE.


After Kibler rolled a 12, Rietzl held them up and yelled "look at this!" and mock checked the dice's corners.


He and Kibler were more than familiar with one another at this point, having played, well, a lot.


"We play in every tournament,"


Except Kibler knew they didn't play in Amsterdam or Honolulu. Suffice to say, these two longtime pros were very familiar with one another.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Kibler.JPG)
*Brian Kibler* 

"Do you shuffle a certain amount of times, or just till you feel like it's good?" Rietzl asked Kibler.


"Till I feel like it," responded the shuffle master.


**Game 1**


On the play Kibler led with an [Ashmouth Hound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ashmouth+Hound) and a [Deranged Assistant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deranged+Assistant), which then let him cast a third turn [Skirsdag Cultist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skirsdag+Cultist) that would prove to be key.


Rietzl neutered the Hound with [Bonds of Faith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonds+of+Faith) and followed up with a Disciple of Grisleback, which was key to activating Morbid and sacrificing any of the Humans that create [Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit) Tokens, but was otherwise pretty pale looking facing down Kibler's newly cast [Pitchburn Devils](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pitchburn+Devils).


Reitzl's second creature, Screetching Bat was allowed an opportunity to transform, and Rietzl took it, turning it into [Stalking Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stalking+Vampire) but not attacking.


Kibler's Cultist threw Ashenmouth Hound at the Disciple and then used [Into the Maw of Hell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Maw+of+Hell) to remove the vampire and attack Rietzl to 10.


Rietzl followed up with an [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim) and [Markov Patrician](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Markov+Patrician), while Kibler milled his second [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) with [Deranged Assistant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deranged+Assistant). He used the Cultist to throw the Assistant at the Patrician and attacked Rietzl to five.


Heavily outgunned on the board and well behind in life, Rietzl took a look at the top of his library before conceding game one.


Kibler 1 Rietzl 0


**Game 2**


On the play for game two, Rietzl was first on the board with a [Village Cannibals](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Village+Cannibals).


"Always a nice creature to have first on the board. [Scathe Zombies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scathe+Zombies)!" Rietzl said.


The Cannibals were good enough to attack past Kibler's [Lantern Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lantern+Spirit), and Rietzl used a splashed [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) to kill a [Moon Heron](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moon+Heron).


The Heron fueled a [Stitched Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stitched+Drake), but even the Drake refused to block the marauding Cannibals as Kibler played around any number of tricks before attacking in with both fliers the next turn.


However, when Kibler passed the turn without any plays, it caused Rietzl to raise an eyebrow. His attack put Kibler to 10, but he was behind in the race.


A Disciple of Grislbrand led Kibler to search for some [Forbidden Alchemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forbidden+Alchemy) and then [Harvest Pyre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harvest+Pyre) the [Village Cannibals](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Village+Cannibals), still in response. [Moment of Heroism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moment+of+Heroism) saved the Cannibals, but tapped Rietzl out in the process.


The fliers got in for five one more time, dropping Rietzl to 6, and then threatened more damage next turn with [Pitchburn Devils](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pitchburn+Devils) and a [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) in hand.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Reitzl.JPG)
*Paul Reitzl* 

"It's getting brutal," Rietzl said, trying to find a way out of the position he found himself in. "I really feel like you have [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley), but I don't think I can arrrggghhh."


Or at least that was an approximation of the groan Rietzl let out before he played an [Elder Cathar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elder+Cathar) and passed with one mana open.


Kibler simply shrugged and attacked with everything.


"Just those?" Rietzl said.


Going through the motions toward the inevitable [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley), Rietzl was dead before showing that he needed a second white mana for the [Fiend Hunter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fiend+Hunter) that could have turned the game around.


Brian Kibler 2 - 0 Paul Rietzl




Round 9 Feature Match - Reid Duke vs. Ricky Sidher
--------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*

"So I've heard you're pretty good at this format," Reid Duke said to Ricky Sidher as they sat down to the match. He's put his finger on something. Sidher has been on a tear in this format ever since winning his grinder at Grand Prix San Diego shattering souls IRL in addition to online under \_\_\_SipItHolla. I admit, not exactly fear-inducing, but still effective.


"Yeah, I guess I am. That's good because I was terrible before this format." Now all this talk about Ricky Sidher was taking the focus off Duke, or by his nom de guerre, reiderrabbit, the current reigning **Magic** Online Champion. Sidher made it to that Championship as well, but Duke took it down.


Both of these players are having great days at 7-1. But a win here would put them in a much better position going into tomorrow.


**Game 1** 


A foil [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) came out on turn two for Duke. "It's the world's most expensive [Ambush Viper](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ambush+Viper)," he quipped while sinking Sidher to 18.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Reid%20Duke.jpg)
*Reid Duke* 

A [Vampire Interloper](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Interloper) was matching the Mage and the two players traded blows despite various comings and goings of creatures. Duke's [Murder of Crows](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder+of+Crows) died a quick death, then the Mage soon after. But that's ok, because their bodies were ripped apart and sewn back together as the very, very large [Skaab Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skaab+Goliath).


It was 12-16 in Sidher's favor after he reset Sidher's board (so to speak) with a Slyer of the Wicked taking out the lone Interloper. Sidher filled his empty zone with [Bloodgift Demon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodgift+Demon) and passed back to Duke, who suited up his [Slayer of the Wicked](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slayer+of+the+Wicked) with a [Blazing Torch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blazing+Torch) and a [Bonds of Faith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonds+of+Faith) making a 5/4 that can't be blocked by Zombies or Vampires and could tap to deal 2 damage.


On the attack, the modified Human rumbled into the red zone and Sidher though hard about blocking, eventually offering the trade of his Demon. But Duke never planned on trading. A [Moment of Heroism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moment+of+Heroism) allowed the [Slay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slay)er to survive and made the totals 19-10 in Duke's favor.


Removal after removal was thrown out on both sides and all that was left standing was a lonely Stitcher's Apprentice for Duke. He shuffled in for 2 damage before a [Geistflame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geistflame) plus flashback took it out.


"What are you at?" Duke asked


"Four." Duke eased back into his seat and dropped a [Doomed Traveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doomed+Traveler) and an [Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker) on the field.


"You just dropped the one card I can't beat." Sidher buried his hand in his chin. It was over soon after.


Reid Duke 1 – 0 Ricky Sidher


The two shuffled up for the match. Sidher chose to draw. "Go ahead, punish me with the [Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker)," he said.


"I'll keep my hand."


Sidher shook his head, "[Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker). I knew it."


**Game 2**


But, in fact, no Stalker. Duke instead started with a [Silver-Inlaid Dagger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silver-Inlaid+Dagger), an [Abbey Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abbey+Griffin) and a [Silverchase Fox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silverchase+Fox). Sidher was having none of that and cast [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley)s on the both of them and cast [Bloodgift Demon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodgift+Demon).


Duke casually laid his [Moorland Haunt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moorland+Haunt), and started using a [Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit) to stab Sidher with a Dagger. After a Demon bash it was 15-16 for Sidher. When he cast Heretic Punishment the next turn it caused Duke a pause. He had no verbal reaction, but he couldn't hide how devastating that card could be to his game plan. He sat and thought.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpaus12/Ricky%20Sidher.jpg)
*Ricky Sidher* 

Sidher lightened the mood by accidentally dropping an [Into the Maw of Hell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Maw+of+Hell). "Well, now you know I have that." The two of them chuckled. But only for a moment. Then Sidher cast a different awesome spell.


"Oh man, look at this!" Duke exclaimed as Sidher cast a [Kessig Cagebreakers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kessig+Cagebreakers).


"The last five cards I've cast may or may not be good." In case you weren't keeping count, the only spells Sidher had cast this game were two [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley)s, [Bloodgift Demon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodgift+Demon), Heretic Punishment and the Cagebreakers. This is Sealed, I promise.


Duke's [Moorland Haunt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moorland+Haunt) was still in the hunt; Duke was still ahead 10-9. But two Punishment activations later, Duke was at 2, and Cagebreakers were in the process of making three attacking 2/2 Wolves.


Yeah. No.


Reid Duke 1 – 1 Ricky Sidher


**Game 3**


Sidher was the aggressor this game starting with a [Skirsdag High Priest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skirsdag+High+Priest) and a [Kessig Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kessig+Wolf) (you know, the one that made the [Kessig Wolf Run](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kessig+Wolf+Run) in less than 12 parsecs). Duke countered with another blank [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) and that lovely [Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker). Sidher sighed.


The two traded spell for creature, spell for creature, until Duke cast a [Murder of Crows](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder+of+Crows). This was the defining play of the game. Sidher thought for a moment, then let it resolve, the made Duke choose between the Crows and the Stalker with a [Tribute to Hunger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribute+to+Hunger). Duke thought. A lot. Eventually, the new 4/4 hit the bin. 16-22 after the [Tribute to Hunger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribute+to+Hunger) resolved.


The next turn Duke revealed his nitro booster to win the race. A Butcher's Cleaver on the Stalker. Sidher immediately realized the one spell that could truly punish his decision to kill the Crows. He could've raced just about anything else. But not a 4/1 Unkillable, unblockable Lifelinker. A few turns later, the scores were 22-10 and no other spells had been cast. Then 23-6.


Sidher drew blank after blank – nothing that would either kill or race the Stalker.


"I should've responded to the Murder." There were some other spells cast, but really, did they matter?


Reid Duke 2 - 1 Ricky Sidher
